in &#39;face&#39;">eɪ</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;s&#39; in &#39;sigh&#39;">s</span><span title="/uː/: &#39;oo&#39; in &#39;goose&#39;">uː</span><span title="&#39;s&#39; in &#39;sigh&#39;">s</span></span>/</a></span></span>,<sup id="cite_ref-eng_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eng-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> <span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ɑː/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;father&#39;">ɑː</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span></span>-/</a></span></span>,<sup id="cite_ref-eng2_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eng2-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> <span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span></span>-/</a></span></span>;<sup id="cite_ref-eng3_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eng3-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Traditional_Chinese_characters" title="Traditional Chinese characters">Chinese</a>&#58; <span lang="zh-Hant">華碩電腦股份有限公司</span>; <a href="/wiki/Pinyin" title="Pinyin">pinyin</a>&#58; <i><span lang="zh-Latn">Huáshuò Diànnǎo Gǔfèn Yǒuxiàn Gōngsī</span></i>; stylized as <b>ASUSTeK</b> or <b>ASUS</b>) is a Taiwanese<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> multinational computer, phone hardware and electronics manufacturer headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Beitou_District" title="Beitou District">Beitou District</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taipei" title="Taipei">Taipei</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>. Its products include <a href="/wiki/Desktop_computers" class="mw-redirect" title="Desktop computers">desktop computers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Laptops" class="mw-redirect" title="Laptops">laptops</a>, <a href="/wiki/Netbook" title="Netbook">netbooks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mobile_phones" class="mw-redirect" title="Mobile phones">mobile phones</a>, networking equipment, monitors, <a href="/wiki/Wireless_router" title="Wireless router">Wi-Fi routers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Projectors" class="mw-redirect" title="Projectors">projectors</a>, <a href="/wiki/Motherboards" class="mw-redirect" title="Motherboards">motherboards</a>, <a href="/wiki/Graphics_cards" class="mw-redirect" title="Graphics cards">graphics cards</a>, <a href="/wiki/Optical_storage" title="Optical storage">optical storage</a>, multimedia products, peripherals, <a href="/wiki/Wearables" class="mw-redirect" title="Wearables">wearables</a>, <a href="/wiki/Server_(computing)" title="Server (computing)">servers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Workstation" title="Workstation">workstations</a> and tablet PCs. The company is also an <a href="/wiki/Original_equipment_manufacturer" title="Original equipment manufacturer">original equipment manufacturer</a> (OEM).
</p><p>As of 2024,<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Asus&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> Asus is the <a href="/wiki/Market_share_of_personal_computer_vendors" title="Market share of personal computer vendors">world's fifth-largest personal computer vendor</a> by unit sales.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Asus appears in <i><a href="/wiki/BusinessWeek" class="mw-redirect" title="BusinessWeek">BusinessWeek</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> "InfoTech 100" and "Asia's Top 10 IT Companies" rankings, and it ranked first in the IT Hardware category of the 2008 Taiwan Top 10 Global Brands survey, with a total brand value of <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US$</a>1.3 <a href="/wiki/Billion" title="Billion">billion</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Asus has a primary listing on the <a href="/wiki/Taiwan_Stock_Exchange" title="Taiwan Stock Exchange">Taiwan Stock Exchange</a> under the ticker code <i>2357</i> and formerly had a secondary listing on the <a href="/wiki/London_Stock_Exchange" title="London Stock Exchange">London Stock Exchange</a> under the ticker code <i>ASKD</i>.
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886046785">.mw-parser-output .toclimit-2 .toclevel-1 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-3 .toclevel-2 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-4 .toclevel-3 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-5 .toclevel-4 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-6 .toclevel-5 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-7 .toclevel-6 ul{display:none}</style><div class="toclimit-3"><meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" /></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Name">Name</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Name"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The company is usually referred to as <i>ASUS</i> or <i>Huáshuò</i> in <a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">Chinese</a> (<a href="/wiki/Traditional_Chinese_characters" title="Traditional Chinese characters">traditional Chinese</a>&#58; <span lang="zh-Hant">華碩</span>; <a href="/wiki/Simplified_Chinese_characters" title="Simplified Chinese characters">simplified Chinese</a>&#58; <span lang="zh-Hans">华硕</span>, literally "Eminence by the Chinese"<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>). According to the company website, the name <i>ASUS</i> originates from <a href="/wiki/Pegasus" title="Pegasus">Pegasus</a>, the winged horse of Greek mythology.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Only the last four letters of the word were used to give the name a high position in alphabetical listings.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
As its marketing <a href="/wiki/Tagline" title="Tagline">taglines</a>, Asus has used <i>Rock Solid. Heart Touching</i> (2003–2009) and subsequently <i>Inspiring Innovation Persistent Perfection</i> (2009–2013). Since 2013, the company's tagline has been <i>In Search of Incredible.</i><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Asus was founded in <a href="/wiki/Taipei" title="Taipei">Taipei</a> in 1989<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> by <a href="/wiki/T.H._Tung" class="mw-redirect" title="T.H. Tung">T.H. Tung</a>, Ted Hsu, Wayne Hsieh and M.T. Liao,<sup id="cite_ref-profile_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-profile-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> all four having previously worked at <a href="/wiki/Acer_Inc." title="Acer Inc.">Acer</a> as <a href="/wiki/Hardware_engineering" class="mw-redirect" title="Hardware engineering">hardware engineers</a>. At this time, Taiwan had yet to establish a leading position in the computer hardware business. <a href="/wiki/Intel_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Intel Corporation">Intel Corporation</a> would supply any new processors to more established companies like <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a> first, and Taiwanese companies would have to wait for approximately six months after IBM received their engineering <a href="/wiki/Prototype" title="Prototype">prototypes</a>. According to company history, Asus created a motherboard prototype for using an <a href="/wiki/Intel_80486" class="mw-redirect" title="Intel 80486">Intel 486</a>, but it had to do so without access to the actual processor. When Asus approached Intel to request a processor to test it, Intel itself had a problem with its own 486 motherboard. Asus solved Intel's problem and it turned out that Asus' motherboard worked correctly without the need for further modification. Since then, Asus was receiving Intel engineering samples ahead of its competitors.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In September 2005, Asus released the first <a href="/wiki/PhysX" title="PhysX">PhysX</a> accelerator card.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> In December 2005, Asus entered the LCD TV market with the TLW32001 model.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> In January 2006, Asus announced that it would cooperate with <a href="/wiki/Lamborghini" title="Lamborghini">Lamborghini</a> to develop the VX laptop series.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 9 March 2006, Asus was confirmed as one of the manufacturers of the first <a href="/wiki/Ultra-Mobile_PC" class="mw-redirect" title="Ultra-Mobile PC">Microsoft Origami</a> models, together with <a href="/wiki/Samsung_Electronics" title="Samsung Electronics">Samsung</a> and <a href="/wiki/Founder_Technology" title="Founder Technology">Founder Technology</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> On 8 August 2006, Asus announced a joint venture with <a href="/wiki/Gigabyte_Technology" title="Gigabyte Technology">Gigabyte Technology</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> On 5 June 2007, Asus announced the launch of the <a href="/wiki/ASUS_Eee_PC" class="mw-redirect" title="ASUS Eee PC">Eee PC</a> at <a href="/wiki/Computex" title="Computex">Computex</a>. On 9 September 2007, Asus indicated support for <a href="/wiki/Blu-ray_Disc" class="mw-redirect" title="Blu-ray Disc">Blu-ray</a>, announcing the release of a BD-ROM/DVD writer PC drive, BC-1205PT.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> ASUS subsequently released several Blu-ray based notebooks.
</p><p>In January 2008, Asus began a major restructuring of its operations, splitting into three independent companies: Asus (focused on applied first-party branded computers and electronics); <a href="/wiki/Pegatron" title="Pegatron">Pegatron</a> (focused on OEM manufacturing of motherboards and components); and <a href="/wiki/Unihan_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Unihan Corporation">Unihan Corporation</a> (focused on non-PC manufacturing such as cases and molding).<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> In the process of the restructuring, a highly criticized pension-plan restructuring effectively zeroed out the existing pension balances. The company paid out all contributions previously made by employees.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 9 December 2008, the <a href="/wiki/Open_Handset_Alliance" title="Open Handset Alliance">Open Handset Alliance</a> announced that Asus had become one of 14 new members of the organization. These "new members will either deploy compatible <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a> devices, contribute significant code to the Android Open-Source Project, or support the ecosystem through products and services that will accelerate the availability of Android-based devices."<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 1 June 2010, Asus spun off Pegatron Corp.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In October 2010, Asus and <a href="/wiki/Garmin" title="Garmin">Garmin</a> announced that they would be ending their smartphone partnership as a result of Garmin deciding to exit the product category.<sup id="cite_ref-taipeitimes271010_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-taipeitimes271010-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> The two companies had produced six Garmin-ASUS branded smartphones over the prior two years.<sup id="cite_ref-taipeitimes271010_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-taipeitimes271010-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In December 2010, Asus launched the world's thinnest notebook, the Asus U36, with Intel processor voltage standard (not low voltage) Intel Core i3 or i5 with a thickness of only 19&#160;mm.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In January 2013, Asus officially ended production of its Eee PC series due to declining sales caused by consumers increasingly switching to <a href="/wiki/Tablet_computer" title="Tablet computer">tablets</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ultrabook" title="Ultrabook">Ultrabooks</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> In April 2022, the company unveiled its new logo.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Operations">Operations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Operations"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:ASUS_US_Headquarters.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/ASUS_US_Headquarters.jpg/220px-ASUS_US_Headquarters.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="150" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/ASUS_US_Headquarters.jpg/330px-ASUS_US_Headquarters.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/ASUS_US_Headquarters.jpg/440px-ASUS_US_Headquarters.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4390" data-file-height="2986" /></a><figcaption>Asus US headquarters in Fremont, California</figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Asus_pro_shop.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Asus_pro_shop.jpg/220px-Asus_pro_shop.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="164" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Asus_pro_shop.jpg/330px-Asus_pro_shop.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Asus_pro_shop.jpg/440px-Asus_pro_shop.jpg 2x" data-file-width="720" data-file-height="537" /></a><figcaption>An Asus shop in Hong Kong</figcaption></figure>
<p>Asus has its headquarters in <a href="/wiki/Beitou_District" title="Beitou District">Beitou District</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taipei" title="Taipei">Taipei</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As of 2009<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Asus&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, Asus had manufacturing facilities in Taiwan (Taipei, <a href="/wiki/Luzhu_District,_Taoyuan" title="Luzhu District, Taoyuan">Luzhu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nangang_District,_Taipei" title="Nangang District, Taipei">Nangang</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guishan_District" title="Guishan District">Guishan</a>), <a href="/wiki/Mainland_China" title="Mainland China">mainland China</a> (<a href="/wiki/Suzhou" title="Suzhou">Suzhou</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chongqing" title="Chongqing">Chongqing</a>), Mexico (<a href="/wiki/Ciudad_Ju%C3%A1rez" title="Ciudad Juárez">Ciudad Juárez</a>) and the Czech Republic (<a href="/wiki/Ostrava" title="Ostrava">Ostrava</a>). The Asus Hi-Tech Park, located in <a href="/wiki/Suzhou" title="Suzhou">Suzhou</a>, covers 540,000&#160;m<sup>2</sup> (5,800,000&#160;sq&#160;ft).<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Asus operates around 50 service sites across 32 countries and has over 400 service partners worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Products">Products</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Products"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Asus' products include 2-in-1s, laptops, tablet computers, desktop computers, <a href="/wiki/Smartphone" title="Smartphone">smartphones</a>, <a href="/wiki/Personal_digital_assistant" title="Personal digital assistant">personal digital assistants</a> (PDAs), <a href="/wiki/Server_(computing)" title="Server (computing)">servers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Computer_monitor" title="Computer monitor">computer monitors</a>, <a href="/wiki/Motherboard" title="Motherboard">motherboards</a>, graphics cards, sound cards, DVD drives, <a href="/wiki/Computer_networking_device" class="mw-redirect" title="Computer networking device">computer networking devices</a>, <a href="/wiki/Computer_case" title="Computer case">computer cases</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electronic_component" title="Electronic component">computer components</a> and <a href="/wiki/Computer_cooling" title="Computer cooling">computer cooling</a> systems.
</p><p>One of Asus main lineup is the <a href="/wiki/Asus_Vivo" title="Asus Vivo">Vivo</a> lineup consisting of laptops (VivoBooks), All-in-Ones (Vivo AiO), desktops (VivoPC), Stick PCs (VivoStick), Mini PCs (VivoMini), smartwatches (VivoWatch), computer mouse (VivoMouse) and tablets (VivoTab).<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Smartphones">Smartphones</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Smartphones"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Asus_ZenFone" title="Asus ZenFone">Asus ZenFone</a></div>
<p>Asus also launched many <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a>-based smartphones, predominantly with <a href="/wiki/Intel" title="Intel">Intel</a> rather than ARM processors and often with two sim slots. Asus is currently very influential in big mobile markets like <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>, and other <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asian</a> countries. It is known as the <a href="/wiki/Asus_ZenFone" title="Asus ZenFone">ZenFone</a> series. Before the ZenFone line, Asus released feature phones such as the <a href="/wiki/Asus_v70" title="Asus v70">Asus v70</a> and smartphones running on <a href="/wiki/Windows_Mobile" title="Windows Mobile">Windows Mobile</a> during the mid-2000s.
</p><p><b>First Generation (2014)</b>
</p>
<ul><li>ZenFone 4 (available in either 4-inch or 4.5-inch variant)</li>
<li>ZenFone 5</li>
<li>ZenFone 6</li></ul>
<p><b>Second Generation (2015)</b>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tablets">Tablets</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Tablets"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:ASUSMeMOPad.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/ASUSMeMOPad.JPG/220px-ASUSMeMOPad.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/ASUSMeMOPad.JPG/330px-ASUSMeMOPad.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/ASUSMeMOPad.JPG/440px-ASUSMeMOPad.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4928" data-file-height="3264" /></a><figcaption>Asus MeMO Pad road show</figcaption></figure>
<p>Two generations of the <a href="/wiki/Google_Nexus_7" class="mw-redirect" title="Google Nexus 7">Nexus 7</a>, manufactured for and branded as <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a>, were announced on 27 June 2012 for release in July 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> On 24 July 2013, Asus announced a successor to the <a href="/wiki/Google_Nexus_7" class="mw-redirect" title="Google Nexus 7">Google Nexus 7</a>. Two days later, it was released.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Asus has also been working with <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a> in developing <a href="/wiki/Windows_8" title="Windows 8">Windows 8</a> convertible tablets.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> In 2013, Asus revealed an Android-based tablet computer that, when attached to a keyboard, becomes a Windows 8 device, which it called the Transformer Book Trio.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> The keyboard can be attached to a third-party monitor, creating a desktop-like experience. Asus is also known for the following tablet computer lines:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/ASUS_Eee_Pad_Transformer" class="mw-redirect" title="ASUS Eee Pad Transformer">Eee Pad Transformer</a></li>
<li>Eee Pad Slider</li>
<li>Eee Slate</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Asus_Memo_Pad_8" title="Asus Memo Pad 8">Memo Pad 8</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Asus_Vivo#VivoTab" title="Asus Vivo">VivoTab</a></li>
<li>ZenPad: 7.0 Z370CG, C 7.0 Z170MG/Z170CG, 8.0 Z380KL, 8.0 Z380C*, S 8.0 Z580CA*, 10 Z300C* (Released 2015); 8.0 Z380M*, Z8 ZT581KL, 3 8.0 Z581KL, 10 Z300M*, 3S 10 Z500M*, Z10 ZT500KL (2016); 3S 8.0 Z582KL, Z8s ZT582KL, 3S 10 Z500KL (2017) (* no <a href="/wiki/Subscriber_identity_module" class="mw-redirect" title="Subscriber identity module">SIM</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-products_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-products-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Eee_line">Eee line</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Eee line"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>From its launch in October 2007 and until the line was discontinued in January 2013, the <a href="/wiki/ASUS_Eee_PC" class="mw-redirect" title="ASUS Eee PC">Eee PC</a> <a href="/wiki/Netbook" title="Netbook">netbook</a> garnered numerous awards, including <a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a> Asia's Product of the Year,<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> Stuff Magazine's Gadget of the Year and Computer of the Year,<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> NBC.com's Best Travel Gadget, Computer Shopper's Best Netbook of 2008, PC Pro's Hardware of the Year, PC World's Best Netbook, and DIME magazine's 2008 Trend Award Winner.
</p><p>Asus subsequently added several products to its Eee lineup, including:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/ASUS_EeeBox_PC" class="mw-redirect" title="ASUS EeeBox PC">EeeBox PC</a>, a compact <a href="/wiki/Nettop" class="mw-redirect" title="Nettop">nettop</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/ASUS_Eee_Top" class="mw-redirect" title="ASUS Eee Top">Eee Top</a>, an all-in-one touchscreen computer housed in an LCD monitor enclosure,</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/ASUS_Eee_Stick" class="mw-redirect" title="ASUS Eee Stick">Eee Stick</a>, a plug-and-play wireless controller for the PC platform that translates users' physical hand motions into corresponding movements onscreen</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/ASUS_Eee_Pad_Transformer" class="mw-redirect" title="ASUS Eee Pad Transformer">Eee Pad Transformer</a>, is a tablet computer that runs the Android operating system.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/ASUS_Eee_Pad_Transformer_Prime" class="mw-redirect" title="ASUS Eee Pad Transformer Prime">Eee Pad Transformer Prime</a>, the successor to the original Transformer.</li></ul>
<p>On 6 March 2009, Asus debuted its Eee Box B202, which <a href="/wiki/PC_Magazine" class="mw-redirect" title="PC Magazine">PCMag</a> saw as "the desktop equivalent of the ASUS EeePC", (the "Asus Eee Box" computer line was later renamed in 2010 to "ASUS EeeBox PC").<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Essentio_Series">Essentio Series</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Essentio Series"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Asus_N55_S_Package.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Asus_N55_S_Package.jpg/220px-Asus_N55_S_Package.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Asus_N55_S_Package.jpg/330px-Asus_N55_S_Package.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Asus_N55_S_Package.jpg/440px-Asus_N55_S_Package.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1456" /></a><figcaption>Asus N55 S Package</figcaption></figure>
<p>Essentio is a line of desktop PCs. As of December&#160;2011<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Asus&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> the line consisted of the CG Series (designed for gaming), the CM series (for entertainment and home use) and the CS and CP slimline series.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Digital_media_receivers">Digital media receivers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Digital media receivers"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Asus sells <a href="/wiki/Digital_media_receiver" class="mw-redirect" title="Digital media receiver">digital media receivers</a> under the name ASUS O!Play.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="GPS_devices">GPS devices</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: GPS devices"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Asus produces the R700T GPS device, which incorporates <a href="/wiki/Traffic_Message_Channel" class="mw-redirect" title="Traffic Message Channel">Traffic Message Channel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Republic_of_Gamers_.28ROG.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Republic_of_Gamers_(ROG)">Republic of Gamers (ROG) <span class="anchor" id="Republic_of_Gamers"></span><span class="anchor" id="ROG"></span></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Republic of Gamers (ROG)"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Asus_Republic_Of_Gamers_Logo.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/d3/Asus_Republic_Of_Gamers_Logo.svg/220px-Asus_Republic_Of_Gamers_Logo.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="41" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/d3/Asus_Republic_Of_Gamers_Logo.svg/330px-Asus_Republic_Of_Gamers_Logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/d3/Asus_Republic_Of_Gamers_Logo.svg/440px-Asus_Republic_Of_Gamers_Logo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="95" /></a><figcaption>Current Republic of Gamers logo</figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Asus_ROG_2015_logo.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Asus_ROG_2015_logo.svg/220px-Asus_ROG_2015_logo.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Asus_ROG_2015_logo.svg/330px-Asus_ROG_2015_logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Asus_ROG_2015_logo.svg/440px-Asus_ROG_2015_logo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="500" /></a><figcaption>Old logo</figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:ASUS_promotional_model_and_Republic-of-Gamers_products_at_Computex_20100603.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/ASUS_promotional_model_and_Republic-of-Gamers_products_at_Computex_20100603.jpg/220px-ASUS_promotional_model_and_Republic-of-Gamers_products_at_Computex_20100603.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="330" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/ASUS_promotional_model_and_Republic-of-Gamers_products_at_Computex_20100603.jpg/330px-ASUS_promotional_model_and_Republic-of-Gamers_products_at_Computex_20100603.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/ASUS_promotional_model_and_Republic-of-Gamers_products_at_Computex_20100603.jpg/440px-ASUS_promotional_model_and_Republic-of-Gamers_products_at_Computex_20100603.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3744" data-file-height="5616" /></a><figcaption>ASUS promotional model and ROG products</figcaption></figure>
<p><b>Republic of Gamers</b> (<b>ROG</b>) is a brand used by ASUS since 2006, encompassing a range of computer hardware, personal computers, peripherals, and accessories. 
</p><p><a href="/wiki/AMD" title="AMD">AMD</a> graphics cards were marketed under the <i>Arez</i> brand due to the <a href="/wiki/Nvidia" title="Nvidia">Nvidia</a>'s <a href="/wiki/GeForce_Partner_Program" title="GeForce Partner Program">GeForce Partner Program</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>In 2013 Asus launched the RAIDR Express, a PCI express-based <a href="/wiki/RAID#Standard_levels" title="RAID">RAID 0</a> SSD subsystem with two SSDs on one PCB.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In January 2022, Asus announced the ROG Flow Z13 during ROG's CES 2022 launch event. Equipped with the high-performance Intel's Core i9 processor and Nvidia's <a href="/wiki/GeForce_30_series" title="GeForce 30 series">GeForce RTX 3050 Ti</a> graphic performance, making the biggest innovation breakthroughs in tablet markets. It is the world's first RTX 30 series computer in tablet form factor.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:ROG_ALLY_-_2.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/ROG_ALLY_-_2.jpg/220px-ROG_ALLY_-_2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="119" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/ROG_ALLY_-_2.jpg/330px-ROG_ALLY_-_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/ROG_ALLY_-_2.jpg/440px-ROG_ALLY_-_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3725" data-file-height="2008" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Asus_ROG_Ally" title="Asus ROG Ally">Asus ROG Ally</a> handheld gaming computer</figcaption></figure>
<p>In June 2023, Asus released the <a href="/wiki/Asus_ROG_Ally" title="Asus ROG Ally">ROG Ally</a>, a handheld device designed to compete with the <a href="/wiki/Steam_Deck" title="Steam Deck">Steam Deck</a>. The Ally possesses a 7-inch (diagonal), <a href="/wiki/1080p" title="1080p">1080p</a> touchscreen display with a 120&#160;Hz refresh rate capability and a <a href="/wiki/16:9_aspect_ratio" title="16:9 aspect ratio">16:9 aspect ratio</a>, versus the Steam Deck's panel that only manages 800p and 60&#160;Hz with a <a href="/wiki/16:10_aspect_ratio" title="16:10 aspect ratio">16:10 aspect ratio</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="The_Ultimate_Force_.28TUF.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Ultimate_Force_(TUF)">The Ultimate Force (TUF)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: The Ultimate Force (TUF)"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:ASUS_TUF_Gaming_X3_20190601.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/ASUS_TUF_Gaming_X3_20190601.jpg/220px-ASUS_TUF_Gaming_X3_20190601.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/ASUS_TUF_Gaming_X3_20190601.jpg/330px-ASUS_TUF_Gaming_X3_20190601.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/ASUS_TUF_Gaming_X3_20190601.jpg/440px-ASUS_TUF_Gaming_X3_20190601.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3200" data-file-height="2400" /></a><figcaption>ASUS TUF Gaming X3</figcaption></figure>
<p><b>The Ultimate Force</b> (<b>TUF</b>) is a brand used by ASUS since about 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> The brand is for Asus affordable, mid-range gaming products.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sound_cards">Sound cards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Sound cards"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Asus released its first sound card, the Xonar DX, in February 2008. The Xonar DX was able to emulate the EAX 5.0 effects through the ASUS GX software while also supporting Open AL and DTS-connect.<sup id="cite_ref-Xonar_DX_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Xonar_DX-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> In July 2008 ASUS launched the Xonar D1, which offered largely similar features to the Xonar DX but connected to the motherboard through the PCI interface instead of the PCI-E ×1 connection of the Xonar DX.<sup id="cite_ref-Xonar_D1_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Xonar_D1-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> ASUS then released the Xonar HDAV 1.3, which was the first solution enabling loss-less HD audio bit streaming to AV receivers.<sup id="cite_ref-ASUS_HDAV_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ASUS_HDAV-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In May 2009, Asus launched the Essence ST sound card, targeted at high-end audiophiles, and featuring 124<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>dB SNR rating and precision audio clock tuning.<sup id="cite_ref-Essence_ST_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Essence_ST-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> In the same month, Asus refreshed the HDAV family by releasing the HDAV 1.3 slim, a card targeted for HTPC users offering similar functionality to HDAV 1.3 but in a smaller form.<sup id="cite_ref-HDAVS_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HDAVS-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> During Computex 2010, ASUS introduced its Xonar Xense, an audio bundle composed of the Xense sound card and a special edition of the Sennheiser PC350 headset.<sup id="cite_ref-Xonar_Xense_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Xonar_Xense-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Xonar_Xense_News_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Xonar_Xense_News-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> In August 2010, ASUS released the Xonar DG sound card targeted at budget buyers and offering 5.1 surround sound support, 105<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>dB SNR rating, support for Dolby headphone and GX 2.5 support for emulating EAX 5.0 technology.<sup id="cite_ref-Xonar_DG_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Xonar_DG-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Xonar_DG_Specs_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Xonar_DG_Specs-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="ASUS_VivoPC_line">ASUS VivoPC line</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: ASUS VivoPC line"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Asus entered the box-PC market with the Vivo PC line in November 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> ASUS VivoPCs come without a pre-installed Windows operating system.
</p><p>On 23 October 2013, ASUS launched two models of VivoPCs in India.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> VivoPC was initially announced with Intel Celeron processor equipped VM40B model. But in India, the company released VivoPC along with a new model called VC60 which is equipped with Intel Core series processors.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Portable_monitors">Portable monitors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Portable monitors"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2013, Asus released the MB168B, a USB 3.0-powered, portable external monitor. The base model shipped with a resolution of <span class="nowrap">1366 × 768</span>, while the MB168B+ had a resolution of <span class="nowrap">1920 × 1080</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-MB168B_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MB168B-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> At the time of its release, the MB168B+ was the only 1080p portable monitor. According to Asus, it is the "world's slimmest and lightest USB monitor".<sup id="cite_ref-MB168B_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MB168B-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Desktop_monitors">Desktop monitors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Desktop monitors"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li>ROG Swift OLED PG27AQDM</li>
<li>ROG Swift OLED PG42UQ</li>
<li>ROG Swift OLED PG48UQ</li>
<li>ROG Swift PG279QM (2560x1440, 240Hz, IPS)</li>
<li>ROG Swift PG27AQN (2560x1440, 360Hz, IPS)</li>
<li>ROG Swift PG279Q<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>ROG Swift PG348Q</li>
<li>ROG Swift PG35VQ<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>ROG Swift PB27UQ</li>
<li>ROG Strix XG27AQ</li>
<li>ROG Strix XG27AQM</li>
<li>ROG Strix XG27AQMR</li>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Motherboards">Motherboards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Motherboards"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Q-connector.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Q-connector.jpg/220px-Q-connector.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="93" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Q-connector.jpg/330px-Q-connector.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Q-connector.jpg/440px-Q-connector.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2714" data-file-height="1147" /></a><figcaption>Q-Connector</figcaption></figure>
<p>Asus motherboards sometimes include a <b>Q-Connector</b> which sits in between the <a href="/wiki/Motherboard" title="Motherboard">motherboard</a> front panel connectors and the front panel cables. The Q-Connector is marked with bigger text than the front panel connectors on the motherboard, as well as protruding from the motherboard, limiting obstruction from <a href="/wiki/Heat_sink" title="Heat sink">heatsinks</a> and other connectors.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Q-connector allows the many front-panel connections to be removed as a single unit for maintenance. This greatly reduces the risk of incorrect connections when reassembling.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_initiatives">Other initiatives</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Other initiatives"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Esports">Esports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Esports"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Asus ROG has been an active advocate for <a href="/wiki/Esports" title="Esports">esports</a>, having established some of their very own professional gaming teams.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In January 2021, ROG announced the establishment of a new esports academy in <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, with plans to scout and train professional gamers for the <a href="/wiki/Counter-Strike:_Global_Offensive" title="Counter-Strike: Global Offensive">Counter-Strike: Global Offensive</a> (CS:GO) PC game.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> The initiative will provide shortlisted gamers with coaching, gaming equipment, and <a href="/wiki/Stipend" title="Stipend">stipends</a> to prepare them for competitive <a href="/wiki/Esports" title="Esports">esports tournaments</a> on both the national and international levels.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_record">Environmental record</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Environmental record"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Green_ASUS">Green ASUS</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Green ASUS"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2000, Asus launched Green ASUS,<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> a company-wide sustainable computing initiative overseen by a steering committee led by Jonney Shih, the Chairman of Asus. According to the company, Asus pursues green policies in "Design, Procurement, Manufacturing, and Marketing."<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recognition">Recognition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Recognition"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2006, Asus obtained IECQ (IEC Quality Assessment System for Electronic Components) and HSPM (Hazardous Substance Process Management) certification for its headquarters and all of its manufacturing sites.<sup id="cite_ref-gms_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gms-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2007, Oekom Research, an independent research institute specializing in corporate responsibility assessment, recognized Asus as a "highly environmental friendly company" in the "Computers, Peripherals and Office Electronics Industry".<sup id="cite_ref-greennews_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-greennews-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In October 2008, Asus received 11 Electronic Product Environmental Assessment Tool (<a href="/wiki/EPEAT" class="mw-redirect" title="EPEAT">EPEAT</a>) Gold Awards for its products,<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> including four of its N-Series notebooks, namely the N10, N20, N50, and N80. In the following month, it received <a href="/wiki/Ecolabel#EU_Ecolabel" title="Ecolabel">EU Flower</a> certification for the same N-Series notebooks at an award ceremony held in Prague.<sup id="cite_ref-greennews_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-greennews-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> In December 2008, <a href="/wiki/Det_Norske_Veritas" class="mw-redirect" title="Det Norske Veritas">Det Norske Veritas</a> conferred the world's first EuP (Energy-using Product) certification for portable notebooks on these machines.<sup id="cite_ref-greennews_84-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-greennews-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recycling_campaign">Recycling campaign</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Recycling campaign"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In April 2008, Asus launched its "PC Recycling for a Brighter Future"<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>
program in collaboration with Intel and with Tsann Kuen Enterprise Co. The program collected more than 1,200 desktop computers, notebooks and CRT/<a href="/wiki/LCD" class="mw-redirect" title="LCD">LCD</a> monitors, refurbished them and donated them to 122 elementary and junior high schools, five aboriginal communities and the <a href="/wiki/Tzu_Chi" title="Tzu Chi">Tzu Chi</a> Stem Cell Center.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversies">Controversies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Controversies"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In September 2008, <i><a href="/wiki/PC_Pro" title="PC Pro">PC Pro</a></i> discovered through a reader that Asus had accidentally shipped laptops that contained cracked and unlicensed software.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> Both physical machines and recovery CDs contained confidential documents from <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a> and other organizations, internal Asus documents, and sensitive personal information including <a href="/wiki/Curriculum_vitae" title="Curriculum vitae">CVs</a>. At the time, an Asus spokesperson promised an investigation at "quite a high level", but declined to comment on how the files got on the machines and recovery media.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> It was demonstrated that an unattended installation of Windows Vista could accidentally copy material from a flash drive with a parameter in the "unattend.xml" file on the personal flash drive being used to script the installation.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Reliable sources"><span title="The material near this tag may rely on an unreliable source. (May 2019)">unreliable source?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>In February 2014, a security vulnerability in the AiCloud functions on a number of Asus routers was compromised to distribute a text file warning of a vulnerability, disclosed in June 2013, allowing the ability to "traverse to any external storage plugged in through the USB ports on the back of the router" via the open internet. Before making the vulnerability public, the researcher was told by Asus that the behavior was "not an issue", but the vulnerability was reportedly patched shortly before the breach.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> The IP addresses of 12,937 routers, and 3,131 AiCloud accounts were also leaked by the hackers.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> The U.S. <a href="/wiki/Federal_Trade_Commission" title="Federal Trade Commission">Federal Trade Commission</a> issued a complaint about the breach for the company's "failure to employ reasonable security practices has subjected consumers to substantial injury", alleging that Asus had also failed to perform basic <a href="/wiki/Penetration_test" title="Penetration test">penetration tests</a>, allowed users to maintain a default admin password for the AiDisk feature and failed to notify users of security updates in a timely fashion. As a result, it was also deemed that Asus had <a href="/wiki/False_advertising" title="False advertising">misled consumers</a> over the security and protection that its routers provided. In February 2016, Asus settled the complaint, agreeing to implement a "comprehensive security program", including independent audits every two years for the next 20 years.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:0_92-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><span class="anchor" id="ShadowHammer"></span>
In March 2019, <a href="/wiki/Kaspersky_Lab" title="Kaspersky Lab">Kaspersky Lab</a> researchers disclosed a <a href="/wiki/Supply_chain_attack" title="Supply chain attack">supply chain attack</a> that affected the Asus Live Update software bundled on its laptops, dubbed <b>ShadowHammer</b>. Kaspersky stated that between June and November 2018, Asus servers had been compromised to distribute a modified version of Live Update, signed with an Asus <a href="/wiki/Digital_signature" title="Digital signature">signature</a>, that contained a <a href="/wiki/Backdoor_(computing)" title="Backdoor (computing)">backdoor</a>. It deployed a further payload if the device's network adapter matched an entry on an internal target list of around 600 <a href="/wiki/MAC_address" title="MAC address">MAC addresses</a>. In response to ShadowHammer, Asus released a patched version of Live Update with improved security measures. Kaspersky and Symantec estimated that between 500,000 and 1 million devices were infected with the backdoor, although Asus attempted to downplay the severity of the breach by noting the extremely targeted nature of the attack. The breach did not affect the similar, identically named software associated with its motherboards.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><span class="anchor" id="Plead"></span>
In April 2019, <a href="/wiki/ESET" title="ESET">ESET</a> disclosed that a group known as BlackTech had performed targeted attacks with malware known as Plead, distributed via the updater for the Asus WebStorage service. ESET stated that the group was likely using a <a href="/wiki/Man-in-the-middle_attack" title="Man-in-the-middle attack">man-in-the-middle attack</a> via a vulnerability in routers, in combination with the updater using an unencrypted <a href="/wiki/Hypertext_Transfer_Protocol" class="mw-redirect" title="Hypertext Transfer Protocol">HTTP</a> connection.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In January 2022, Asus recalled some of its <a href="/wiki/LGA_1700" title="LGA 1700">Z690</a> Maximus Hero motherboards due to a manufacturing flaw, where a RAM <a href="/wiki/Capacitor" title="Capacitor">capacitor</a> was installed backward—causing them to burn out associated <a href="/wiki/MOSFET" title="MOSFET">MOSFETs</a> and prevent the motherboard from detecting memory.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Following the <a href="/wiki/2022_Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine" class="mw-redirect" title="2022 Russian invasion of Ukraine">Russian invasion of Ukraine in 2022</a>, ASUS initially refused to join a widespread withdrawal of businesses from the Russian market. In mid-March, the company did announce it was halting its operations in Russia, following a social media boycott and government pressure.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In April 2023, a post on the PCMasterRace <a href="/wiki/Subreddit" class="mw-redirect" title="Subreddit">subreddit</a> began gaining popularity regarding the user's AMD <a href="/wiki/Ryzen_7000" class="mw-redirect" title="Ryzen 7000">Ryzen 7 7800X3D</a> CPU, which had visible burning, along with the <a href="/wiki/CPU_socket" title="CPU socket">socket</a> of the Asus motherboard.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> This sparked the attention of both people interested in PCs, who initially thought it was an issue with the 3D V-Cache Technology (as there had been previous user reports similar to this incident),<sup id="cite_ref-:1_101-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> as well as enthusiast YouTube channels such as Gamers Nexus, who ran tests to successfully recreate the burning of their CPU.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> They realised that the cause of the burning was due to a voltage error in the BIOS. In May, Asus responded to the incidents by releasing a <a href="/wiki/Beta_software" class="mw-redirect" title="Beta software">Beta</a> BIOS, which was supposed to fix the error. However, not only did the new BIOS not fix the issue; by installing it, the user voided their warranty as it was a Beta BIOS, which Asus clearly stated in the BIOS's description.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_102-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> Later that month, Asus responded to the public backlash by reversing course, releasing a statement informing users that they will continue to honor warranty on motherboards that have been updated to beta BIOS versions, as well as extend motherboard warranty coverage to uses of <a href="/wiki/AMD_EXPO" class="mw-redirect" title="AMD EXPO">AMD EXPO</a>, <a href="/wiki/Intel_XMP" class="mw-redirect" title="Intel XMP">Intel XMP</a>, and <a href="/wiki/DOCP" class="mw-redirect" title="DOCP">DOCP</a> memory overclocking technologies.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<li id="cite_note-12"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-12">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1215172403"><cite id="CITEREFMaks" class="citation web cs1 cs1-prop-foreign-lang-source">Maks, Kurmaz. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20070102235613/http://www.hw.by/events/ASUS.html">"Интервью с ASUS"</a> &#91;Interview with ASUS&#93;. <i>hw.by</i> (in Russian). Archived from <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.hw.by/events/ASUS.html">the original</a> on 2 January 2007<span class="reference-accessdate">. [Translation: The ASUS company formed in 1989 ... Its name is formed from the English word "PegASUS" ...
